Report from Gansu Province: Hopes for Investment and Cultivation in the Border Region; Vast Land and Sparse Population Lead to Foreign Covetousness; It is Imperative to Seize the Opportunity for Development to Remedy the Situation

A Central News Agency report states that municipal authorities in various provinces have recently become increasingly aware that the growing number of unemployed people within their jurisdictions has had a significant impact on social economy and local security. They generally believe that the best way to alleviate this unemployment panic is to transport the unemployed to the border regions for cultivation. The border regions such as the Northwest have vast lands and sparse populations. Border authorities and local people also hope that the unemployed from the interior will quickly go to cultivate. A Central News Agency reporter yesterday met Mr. Zhang, a friend who had just returned to Shanghai from Gansu, who told him the following:

Vast Land and Sparse Population: Inviting Covetousness

Mr. Zhang has worked in the transportation sector in Gansu for four years. In his spare time, he has paid attention to investigating local customs. According to him, the northwestern border provinces have vast areas, several times larger than the southeastern provinces, but the population is sparse. In remote areas, one can walk for dozens of miles without seeing a single person. As a result, the land is barren. The land is full of gold but no one to collect it, which has aroused foreign covetousness. In recent years, border incidents have occurred from time to time. Although the reasons are different, the vast land and sparse population, which aroused foreign covetousness, is the biggest factor. Moreover, the sparse population in the border region violates the principle of national defense. Therefore, to consolidate the border region, we must first encourage immigration.

Local Hopes: Investment and Cultivation

The border provinces and regions, due to the backwardness of culture and economy, deeply hope that people from the interior will go to invest and develop. Although the slogan of calling for investment in the interior has been repeatedly heard in the Shanghai banking community, it has not yet benefited the border region. The people of the country know the wealth of the Northwest and other places, so they are eager for the financial and industrial circles of Shanghai to go and invest. At the same time, the local people also deeply know that to prosper the local area, the population must be increased. In the southeast and other places, due to the sluggish market, there are too many people for too few jobs, and there is often an unemployment panic. The border region is suffering from a sparse population. The unemployed in the interior can go to cultivate, which can solve the unemployment panic, prosper the border area, and consolidate national defense. It is a win-win situation.

Rich Profits and Convenient Transportation

Mr. Zhang also said that the Northwest border region is rich in resources and should set up industries and factories. The price of goods and raw materials in the border region is very low. Manufacturing goods locally for export can greatly reduce costs and make rich profits. Moreover, transportation facilities in the Northwest have also gradually developed in recent years, and transportation will not be greatly affected. If people in the interior can go to cultivate in groups, the local area will gradually prosper, and transportation facilities will also inevitably develop. It can be asserted that if everyone waits for the border transportation to be convenient before investing and cultivating, the border region will never be developed.

Current Key Point: Setting Up Information Centers

The customs and customs of the border area are very similar to those of the interior, and immigrants will not feel great inconvenience when they go there. In order to facilitate the people of the interior to start in the border area, I think we should set up information centers in Shanghai, Nanjing and other places for the people of the interior to inquire about various matters when going to the border area, such as the route, expenses, customs of the border area, living conditions, etc. This information center should contain an introduction. Those who go there will not hesitate to move forward after receiving this introduction before departure. At the same time, I also hope that state-owned transportation agencies will give preferential treatment to people going to the border area in terms of travel expenses, etc.

Incidents Involving Jianghai Steamships

Sanxing

The Sanxing Shipping Company's Sanxing ship, loaded with goods from Tianjin to Shanghai on the 16th. It did not leave Dagu until 2:00 AM, but because of the low water level, it ran aground in front of Pier No. 6. The hull hit the pier, damaging one of the teeth of the pier and destroying one of the customs buoys there, resulting in great losses. After the accident, people have been sent to inspect the ship. The ship was only able to get out of the ground and set sail when the tide rose that night. There was a telegram to Shanghai yesterday reporting the incident.

Youmu

The Youmu ship of the China United Wharf Warehouse Company, loaded with 1,400 tons of salt in Haizhou, and sailed to the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. On the 18th, when the ship arrived 40 miles downstream of Shashi, the river was at low tide, and the ship was heavily loaded, it suddenly ran aground. The ship was drafting 15 feet, and the bottom of the ship was stuck in the mud and could not be moved. The shipowner telegraphed the Shanghai company for help. The company has agreed with Sanbei Company. Fortunately, the small Sanbei ship was unloading its cargo in Yichang. Yesterday, the company had rented the small Sanbei ship to rush to the downstream of Shashi to rescue the ship and unload the salt. The daily rent is 800 yuan. Youmu plans to wait until all the salt in the cabins is unloaded before dragging the ship out of the ground.

Jiang'an

The Jiang'an ship of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which was loaded with cargo from the Pinghan Railway, sailed from Hankou to Shanghai and had to be unloaded at the new wharf in Yangjiadu. When the ship was docking, it was just in time for the high tide (it was during the Great Tide period), and the water was rapid and the waves were huge. The hull was forced to avoid the small ships on the Huangpu River, and it collided with the Yangjiadu Wharf, damaging one or two floating bridges on the wharf at that time. After the accident, it was reported to the bureau yesterday, and the head office has sent people to inspect the wharf and prepare for repairs.

Tonghe

The Tonghe ship of the Dalu Industrial Company collided with the Shen'ai ship of the Yilong Foreign Company near Zhenjiang. The Tonghe ship was severely damaged, the pulley of the steering gear has been broken, the screws on the right side of the front hull have been loosened, and it has been stranded for four days. The technicians sent there could not repair it, and the front cabin has been flooded with one inch per hour. The salt in the ship has been damaged. After receiving the telegram from Shanghai, Mr. Fang, the director of Dalu Shipping, went to Zhenjiang to inspect the ship and discuss rescue methods. The shipowner is a Russian, Vinoscov. Dalu Company, because the Western shipowner of the Chunhe ship was replaced by the Chinese, Huang Yajun, the technology and driving skills are better than the Westerners. Tonghe ship also plans to use Chinese people, but unexpectedly, it has already caused trouble and suffered great damage.

Special Freight Rates for Joint Transportation of Cotton on the Beijing-Shanghai and Jinpu Railways

The Beijing-Shanghai Railway and the Jinpu Railway have submitted to the Ministry of Railways a request to reduce the freight rate for the joint transportation of ordinary and inferior cotton. The ministry has been instructed to approve the following: For the Jinpu Railway section, the freight rate will be reduced by 15% for distances within 300 kilometers, 20% for distances between 301 and 600 kilometers, and 30% for distances of 601 kilometers and above. All calculations will be based on the original freight rates for the corresponding grades of cotton. For shipments starting from Tianjin and directly reaching Pukou, the freight rate will still be calculated based on a distance of 800 kilometers. For the Beijing-Shanghai Railway section, the freight rate will be reduced by 20% based on the original freight rates for the corresponding grades of cotton. Furthermore, the joint transportation progressive reduction method will apply to freight rates for both the Beijing-Shanghai and Jinpu Railway sections. The trial implementation will begin on October 1st of this year and will last for six months.

Municipal Public Security Bureau Captures the Murderer in the Xuan Sheng Case; The Main Culprit Wang Zhensheng and Mao Yonghu Zhao Yunpeng; The Murder Weapon Handgun Has Also Been Obtained and Proven

According to a Central News Agency report, the person in charge of the Municipal Public Security Bureau stated yesterday that after the Xuan Sheng case of the Japanese resident occurred on July 10 of this year, the municipal government ordered the Public Security Bureau to arrest the murderer and pay special attention to protecting Japanese residents. After receiving the order, the bureau repeatedly ordered its subordinates to widely purchase information and set a time limit for solving the case. It also offered a heavy reward in order to capture the murderer as soon as possible. Last month, several suspects who had premeditated the assassination were arrested. The interrogation revealed that they were related to the Xuan Sheng Zhongshan case. They were temporarily handed over to the Public Concession Police Department for investigation for reference. Later, the Police Department sent them back to the bureau. On the one hand, the bureau resumed tracking down other clues, and on the 15th and 16th of this month, it successively arrested the main criminals Mao Yonghu and Zhao Yunpeng in the case in Nanshi. According to the confession, the main culprit Wang Zhensheng was still living in Zhabei. The bureau then sent detectives to capture Wang at his address at midnight on the 17th. After taking him back to the bureau, he was interrogated. He revealed that the murder weapon handgun was thrown into the garbage pile under the Hu Family Wooden Bridge near Qimei Road. The bureau then sent personnel to accompany Wang to the Hu Family Wooden Bridge to retrieve the murder weapon handgun. The bureau then sent personnel to take the gun to the Public Concession Police Department for inspection. It was verified that the gun was a revolver handgun, using Brownell automatic pistol bullets, with six bullets loaded, one bullet had been fired, and the shell was still in the gun, and there were five unfired bullets. It was indeed the murder weapon handgun in the case.

New Second Public Bus Route Opened in South Shanghai; Diesel Buses Will Be Used Starting Today; Running Between Shiliupu and Caohejing; Yesterday Invited All Sectors to Visit

The Municipal Public Works Bureau's Public Bus Management Office has opened a new second bus route between Caohejing and Shiliupu, using new-style diesel public buses with exceptionally comfortable seating and affordable fares. The route is scheduled to open this morning. Yesterday, a special invitation was extended to all sectors to visit and try out the buses, with tea and refreshments served at the Huang Family Garden. During the event, Director Xu Peihuang of the bureau gave a report. The details are recorded below.

Inviting Guests

The city-run second public bus route is scheduled to open at 6:00 AM this morning. The Public Works Bureau and the Public Bus Management Office specially hosted a visit for all sectors at Huang Family Garden in Caohejing at 2:30 PM yesterday. The bureau provided 12 new-style diesel public buses to welcome and transport guests at the Heping Road Station in Laoximen. Yesterday happened to be Saturday afternoon, and the weather was fine, so many people went, totaling 300 people from political, business, and press circles. After arriving at Huang Family Garden, they first toured the garden for a week, and then tea and refreshments were served in the thatched cottage of Dalichun Restaurant. Director Xu Peihuang of the Public Works Bureau gave a report. The event ended at 4:00 PM, and the guests were transported back to Heping Road Station by the original buses and dispersed.

Xu's Report

Director Xu said at the reception, "Distinguished guests, the second Caohejing route will be opened today. I am honored to have your presence. Our bureau's public buses have been operating for two years. Taking advantage of the opening of the new route, we are holding this event at Huang Garden, providing some tea and refreshments to express our welcome and briefly report on the general situation of the past two years since the opening. Looking at the transportation tools in this city, except for the city ferries, most of them are commercially operated. Even the public buses in the South Shanghai area were previously commercially operated. However, due to poor management, they lost the trust of the citizens, resulting in failure. After that, the transportation in the Nanshi area became inconvenient again. Therefore, our bureau submitted a request to the municipal government to change to city-run buses. The intention is to supplement the inadequacy of existing transportation tools, and the premise is entirely to facilitate citizens' transportation. It is not for the purpose of making profits. Therefore, even when the city treasury is stretched, we still carry out this grand wish with determination. Fortunately, with the guidance of the mayor and the support of all sectors and car dealers, we were able to establish it. I should express my twelve-point gratitude. The Public Bus Management Office adopts strict scientific management in terms of personnel, affairs, and materials. For example, drivers, ticket sellers, and inspectors are all recruited through examinations and given appropriate training. Then, they are promoted and demoted step by step, so that service personnel have the desire to compete and improve work efficiency. For mechanical aspects, such as management, repair, and assembly, all three projects are supervised and handled by experienced supervisors, researched and improved without any slack. For the purchase and consumption of materials, accessories, and oil, there is also reasonable management and detailed statistics to ensure that no funds are wasted and to strive for frugality. Over the past two years, although we have established a foundation, there are still many shortcomings. I hope that all sectors will give us guidance." Xu continued, "After the establishment of the Public Bus Management Office, we first operated the first and third routes. The first route is an important traffic route between Laoximen and Longhua, especially during the spring incense season. The third route is a circular route around the city. The establishment of this route is to supplement the inadequacy of transportation tools on that route. Then, we added the fourth and eleventh routes. The fourth route is also a circular route, starting from Dapu Bridge, passing Lujiabang, Limallu, Minguo Road, and returning to the original Dapu Bridge. The establishment of this route is based on the fact that there are no transportation tools near Xieqiao west and Lujiabang Road, and citizens feel very inconvenient to travel. Therefore, we developed it to meet the needs. According to the latest statistics, the number of passengers on that route is increasing day by day, almost comparable to the third route. The eleventh route is Pudong Avenue, connecting the north and south traffic, and is intended to cross the Shangchuan and Shangnan transportation companies, so that passengers can reduce their wading. Since its opening, it has been well received by the citizens of Pudong. Now, in the new western district of South Shanghai in this city, the number of residents has been increasing in recent years. At the same time, many citizens who serve in the special zone live in Caohejing. Recently, gardens and factories in the Caohejing area have been increasing day by day. Every holiday, Chinese and Westerners traveling to the suburbs can be seen on the road. However, the lack of fast and convenient transportation tools is very inconvenient. A year ago, our bureau had the motive to add a route from Caohejing to Laoximen and Shiliupu. In order to reduce the burden on passengers, it is not economical to use gasoline vehicles for operation. Therefore, we decided to use diesel engines for the 12 new vehicles we added. As for how to make the appearance of the body and the interior of the car more beautiful, comfortable, and safe, we have researched and improved them to meet the expectations of the citizens. Today, we are honored to have guests from all walks of life come to visit, and we are grateful to Mr. Huang Jinyong, the owner of the garden, for generously lending his private garden as the place for our bureau's reception, as well as the general public and car dealers like Hejin Company for trusting our bureau and sincerely supporting us. I am extremely honored and would like to thank you all."

Low Fares

The vehicles used by the bureau are the Hejin Company's Da Mengtian new diesel engine vehicles (reportedly built by Dachang Machinery Factory). The body is wide, each weighing two tons and carrying four tons. The exterior is light blue and light yellow, while the interior is yellow, with deep blue curtains hanging down, which is very beautiful. The leather seats are also spacious and comfortable, and can carry 45 passengers. The cost of each vehicle is 15,000 yuan, and more than a dozen have been purchased, with ten dedicated to the new route. The route runs from Shiliupu, Limalu, Damatou Street, through Dadongmen, across the city, via Qiaojiabang Road, Ninghe Road, Penglai Road, out of Laoximen, to Xieqiao, along Xietu Road, to Jinji Road, detour via Xujiahui, and to Caohejing Town. The entire route is 21 kilometers long, divided into 12 stations, and it takes one hour for the car to reach. A bus runs every twelve minutes. The fare is 5 cents from Damatou to Xiaodongmen, 7 cents to Dadongmen, 9 cents to Qiaojiabang, 11 cents to Public Security Bureau, 13 cents to Laoximen, 18 cents to Xieqiao, 24 cents to Luban Road, 30 cents to Damuqiao, 36 cents to Jinji Road, 36 cents to Tianyao Bridge, 42 cents to Tianyao Bridge Road, 48 cents to Zhongshan Road, 54 cents to Cao's Cemetery, and 60 cents to Caohejing. It is also stipulated that the fare for each station east of Laoximen is 5 cents, and the fare for each station west of Laoximen is 6 cents.

The Central Government Revised the Regulations for Surveying and Reporting Disasters and Crop Failures; Orders All Provinces and Cities to Comply; The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Transferred the Order to the Farmers' Association for Notification

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau received the Regulations for Surveying and Reporting Disasters and Crop Failures issued by the Executive Yuan yesterday. After receiving the order, the bureau specially instructed the Municipal Farmers' Association to transfer the order to all district farmers' associations and members for notification. The instructions and regulations for surveying and reporting disasters and crop failures are recorded below.

Order to the Municipal Farmers' Association

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau instructed the Municipal Farmers' Association yesterday, "According to the Municipal Government's Instruction No. 9886, the Executive Yuan's Instruction No. 4785 states, 'The Regulations for Surveying and Reporting Disasters and Crop Failures have been formulated and promulgated and should be immediately notified for implementation. The revised Regulations for Surveying and Reporting Disasters promulgated on February 24, 1934, should be abolished at the same time. In addition to distributing the order separately, a copy of the Regulations for Surveying and Reporting Disasters is enclosed for your information and for transfer to your subordinates for notification. This order.' etc. Enclosed is a copy of the Regulations for Surveying and Reporting Disasters. Upon receipt, the Municipal Government issued Instruction No. 9886. This order is hereby issued. In addition to distributing the order separately, a copy of the original regulations is enclosed for the bureau's compliance. This order." etc. A copy of the Regulations for Surveying and Reporting Disasters is enclosed. In addition to distributing the regulations separately, a copy of the original regulations is enclosed for the association's compliance. This order.

Regulations for Surveying and Reporting

The Regulations for Surveying and Reporting Disasters and Crop Failures are as follows: (Article 1) These Regulations shall be followed for surveying and reporting water, drought, wind, hail, insect damage, and other disasters in various places. (Article 2) In the event of a disaster affecting land in a county or city, the county or city government shall first conduct a survey and report the disaster situation to the provincial government for verification. (Article 3) After receiving the report of a disaster in a county or city, the provincial government shall immediately dispatch personnel to conduct a joint survey with the county or city. The names of the affected villages, the area of the land, and the severity of the disaster in each place shall be listed in a clear report, along with a sketch map of the affected land, and submitted to the provincial government for approval. Disasters in cities and special administrative regions directly under the Executive Yuan shall be surveyed and approved locally by the respective city governments and competent authorities without the need for provincial re-survey. (Article 4) The deadline for reporting disasters is the day before the beginning of autumn for summer disasters and the day before the beginning of winter for autumn disasters, except for temporary emergencies that cause disasters. The deadline may be appropriately extended in areas with a later climate. (Article 5) The deadline for surveying disasters is ten days for the initial survey of locusts and other disasters in counties and cities. Wind, hail, water disasters, and other emergencies shall be surveyed immediately, but no later than three days. The deadline for re-survey by counties and cities and committees is fifteen days. (Article 6) If a disaster continues to occur in a place, except for drought and locust disasters, which shall be surveyed and reported within the original time limit, other continuing disasters that occur within fifteen days of the original disaster report shall be included in the original survey and report. If the initial survey deadline has passed and a severe disaster occurs, a new survey and report may be initiated. (Article 7) When surveying summer disasters in a place, if the situation is relatively light and autumn crops can still be planted, the number of fractions shall be determined at the time of the autumn harvest. If autumn crops are not planted in the meantime, the number of fractions shall be determined at the time of the summer disaster. (Article 8) The number of fractions approved by the provincial and municipal governments shall be calculated from the time when the total harvest of the affected land throughout the year is less than half of the average harvest. If the harvest is more than half of the average harvest, it shall not be considered a disaster. (Article 9) If land taxes are to be reduced or exempted in an area affected by a disaster, the standards and extent shall be handled in accordance with the Regulations for the Reduction and Exemption of Land Taxes. (Article 10) If relief is required in an area affected by a disaster, the provincial or municipal government shall verify and allocate funds for relief and notify the Ministries of Interior and Finance for record. However, in the event of a major disaster or a wide area affected by a disaster, the confirmed situation of the disaster may be notified to the Ministries of Interior and Finance, which shall request the Central Government to provide subsidies as appropriate. (Article 11) A county magistrate who surveys and reports disasters and crop failures and commits one of the following acts shall be punished in accordance with the Law on the Punishment of Public Officials: (1) Failure to immediately survey a disaster in a place, or failure to report it after surveying, or making a false report. (2) Leaving the reported disaster land for survey and approval of fractions, failing to order the planting of crops, and delaying agricultural affairs. (3) Exceeding the time limit prescribed in these Regulations for initial and re-surveys. (Article 12) A member of the survey committee who commits one of the acts described in Clauses 1 and 3 of the preceding article shall be punished in accordance with the provisions of the preceding article. (Article 13) These Regulations shall be implemented immediately upon promulgation.

China Insurance Society Held Annual Meeting Yesterday, Urging Pan and Wang to Speak

The China Insurance Society held its first annual meeting at the Shanghai Bankers' Association yesterday afternoon, starting at 1:00 PM. Those in attendance included Mr. Pan Gongzhan and Mr. Wang Yunwu, who were invited by the society to speak, as well as Mao Yun, representative of the Municipal Party Department, Xu Kesheng, representative of the Insurance Trade Association, and local and out-of-town members Song Hanzhang, Li Quanshi, Zhang Sumin, Yang Yongchao, Chen Jiaxuan, Ding Xuenong, Hu Yongqi, Zhang Mingxin, Wang Xiaowen, Fan Baohua, and dozens of others. Song Hanzhang, Hu Yongqi, and Xiang Xinwu were publicly elected as the presidium. After the ceremonial proceedings, Chairman Song Hanzhang first reported on the establishment of the society and the progress of its work over the past year. Luo Beichen, the general manager of the annual meeting preparatory committee, reported on the preparation process. Then, Mr. Pan Gongzhan was invited to speak, elaborating on labor insurance in detail and encouraging the society to promote its implementation. Following him, Mr. Wang Yunwu spoke, expressing his strong agreement with the society's suggestion to add insurance materials to textbooks and detailing the group insurance plan provided by the Commercial Press. Mao Yun and Xu Kesheng, representing the Municipal Party Department and the Insurance Trade Association, respectively, delivered speeches with much encouragement. It was decided to read two papers: one by Chen Jiaxuan on labor legislation insurance issues and the other by Fan Baohua on cooperation strategies between life insurance and bank savings. Afterwards, the articles of association were discussed and revised. The meeting adjourned with a photo session at 6:00 PM. Details are recorded below.

Report on Society Affairs

Chairman Song Hanzhang reported on the society's activities over the past year, including: (1) Petitioning the Ministry of Education to issue a circular to include insurance education materials in elementary school textbooks; (2) The society and a course on insurance in Shanghai; (3) Publishing an insurance quarterly; (4) Petitioning the Ministry of Education and sending a letter to the China-British Boxer Indemnity Scholarship Fund's Tsinghua University to dispatch insurance students to study abroad; (5) Petitioning the Legislative Yuan and the Ministry of Finance to revise the Provisional Income Tax Regulations to include life insurance as a tax-exempt item; (6) Seeking members; (7) The society encouraging students studying abroad to study insurance; (8) The society and the Shanghai Insurance Trade Association jointly writing to various universities and specialized schools, requesting the establishment of insurance courses; (9) Preparing for academic insurance lectures; (10) Preparations for the society's annual meeting.

Articles of Association Adopted

The articles of association adopted by the general meeting yesterday are recorded as follows: Chapter 1, General Provisions: Article 1, The name of this society is the China Insurance Society. Article 2, The purpose of this society is to study insurance theory and promote the insurance industry. Article 3, The general headquarters of this society shall be located in Shanghai, and branch societies may be organized in various provinces, cities, and important foreign locations, subject to the approval of the board of directors. Chapter 2, Members: Article 4, The members of this society are divided into two categories: individual members and group members. I. Individual members: Any citizen of the Republic of China who studies insurance or is engaged in the insurance business may become an individual member of this society upon the introduction of two members of this society and with the approval of the board of directors. II. Group members: Any public or private legal entity insurance group of the Republic of China may become a group member of this society upon the introduction of two members of this society and with the approval of the board of directors. Group members shall nominate one person as their representative. Chapter 3, Society Affairs: Article 5, The society's affairs are as follows: (1) Studying insurance theory; (2) Investigating insurance practices; (3) Compiling insurance statistics; (4) Drafting insurance clauses; (5) Training insurance personnel; (6) Holding insurance lectures; (7) Publishing insurance books and newspapers; (8) Establishing an insurance library; (9) Organizing various insurance research groups. Chapter 4, Organization: Section 1, Board of Directors: Article 6, This society shall have a board of directors composed of fifteen directors, and nine standing directors shall be elected by the directors to handle daily affairs. The board of directors shall have one chairman, who shall be elected by the standing directors. Article 7, Directors shall be elected by mail, with those receiving the most votes being elected, and those with the next highest number of votes being alternate directors. Article 8, The term of office for directors is three years, with one-half being re-elected each year, and they may be re-elected. Article 9, The chairman represents the society externally and presides over all society affairs internally. Article 10, When the chairman is unable to perform his duties, he may entrust one of the standing directors to act on his behalf. Article 11, This society shall have one secretary and one accountant, who shall be appointed from among the directors. Section 2, Honorary Directors: Article 12, Those who have made special contributions to insurance academics, the insurance industry, or the society's affairs may be recommended as honorary directors of this society upon approval by the board of directors. Section 3, Branch Societies: Article 13, Branch societies shall have one general manager and several managers, who shall be elected by the members' general meeting of the branch society for a term of one year and may be re-elected. Chapter 5, Meetings: Article 14, The meetings of this society are divided into the following three types: I. Members' Annual Meeting; II. Board of Directors Meeting; III. Standing Directors' Meeting. Article 15, The annual meeting shall be held once a year and convened by the board of directors one month in advance. When necessary, a special members' meeting may be convened by a resolution of the board of directors. Article 16, The board of directors shall hold a regular meeting once a month. Article 17, The standing directors' meeting shall be convened by the chairman at any time. Chapter 6, Rights and Obligations of Members: Article 18, Individual members and group members have the right to elect and be elected and to enjoy all the rights of this society. Article 19, The admission fee for individual members is five yuan per person, and the admission fee for group members is one hundred yuan per group. The annual membership fee is five yuan per person for individual members and one hundred yuan per group for group members. Article 20, The membership fees shall be used as the society's fund and shall not be used for other purposes without a resolution of the board of directors. Chapter 7, Supplementary Provisions: Article 21, If there are any matters not covered in these articles of association, they may be amended by a resolution of the annual meeting. Article 22, After these articles of association are adopted, they shall be submitted to the competent authority for record and shall take effect.

Resolutions Passed

The discussion of various proposals commenced immediately after. (1) Submitting a proposal to the Legislative Yuan to compile a labor insurance law; resolved and passed. (2) The society should petition the Legislative Yuan to pass the insurance law as soon as possible; resolved and passed. (3) The society should petition the Ministry of Industry to implement insurance regulations; resolved and passed. (4) Suggesting that the government employ life insurance experts to compile a national mortality table based on our country's experience; resolved and passed. (5) The society should establish a library as soon as possible; resolved and passed, to be handled by the next board of directors. (6) Raising funds for the society; resolved, to be handled by the next board of directors. (7) Publishing a China Insurance Yearbook; resolved, to be handled by the next board of directors. (8) Contacting other economic and academic organizations to hold joint annual meetings; resolved, to be handled by the next board of directors. (9) Compiling an insurance practitioner curriculum; resolved, reserved. (10) Writing to the Shanghai Insurance Trade Association to request that the life insurance industry contribute a reasonable subsidy for the insurance quarterly's promotional expenses; resolved and passed.

French National Stahl Trafficking Drugs, French Authorities Issue Arrest Warrant

The "North China Daily News" reports that earlier this month, a Chinese woman named Wen Mali was found to have concealed 48 pounds of morphine in a hidden compartment of her luggage while traveling from Shanghai to the United States, intending to smuggle it into Los Angeles. Upon the ship's arrival at the port, both the person and the contraband were seized. According to her confession, the morphine was supplied by Stahl of the Baolong Hospital in Shanghai. Stahl, a Frenchman from Alsace, has been working at Baolong Hospital as an inspector (mainland reports claim that he was the chief accountant) for many years. After news of Stahl's involvement in morphine smuggling came out, the hospital dismissed him from his position several days ago. His whereabouts are now unknown. Currently, the Public Concession, the French Concession, and the Shanghai Municipal Government's police authorities are all seeking to arrest him to investigate everything. They have been visiting various locations for days, but have not found any trace of him. It is now believed that he is still hiding in or near Shanghai and will likely be apprehended soon. Even if he flees to other cities, it will be difficult for him to escape justice, as authorities around the world are now paying attention to him. At the same time, authorities are also paying attention to other foreigners in Shanghai who are suspected of being involved in local morphine manufacturing plants and morphine supply sources. One suspect who recently died in Shanghai is said not to be part of the European drug trafficking group associated with Brandesstedter. Many members of that group, including Lian Bai, have recently fled Shanghai. One of them, Weis Muller, is reportedly in Central America, and the American authorities are currently tracking his whereabouts. The European group is financially strong and has been operating in Europe for six or seven years before its key figures fled to the East. Bai was the group's Far East manager in Shanghai. Its headquarters in New York has been operating for three years. In May of this year, Bai was forced to flee to Europe. Not long after, he secretly went to Cuba, but was expelled by Havana authorities at the end of August. He later committed suicide on the Orient Line's "Eastern" ship in New York Harbor on September 4. It is believed that Wen Mali's morphine smuggling case implicated him, and the California court intended to arrest and interrogate him. It is reported that the international opium and narcotic smuggling organization was broken up under the personal direction of the U.S. Secretary of the Treasury. The discovery of Wen Mali's smuggling is part of this operation. The woman is Cantonese and was a nurse at Baolong Hospital. The retail value of the morphine she was carrying was $50,000 USD, enough for one million medicinal doses, enough to kill 500,000 people. The woman is currently awaiting trial. According to a telegram from the United States, she is suffering from a severe case of influenza. The woman has a younger sister who currently lives in Los Angeles.

The "Great American Evening Post" reports that in the case of Wen Mali's morphine smuggling into the United States, in addition to the French national Stahl, who is involved in the case and has now fled, another foreigner is also implicated. The three police authorities in the city are currently hunting for him. Authorities do not want to announce his name or nationality, but it is known that he is not American and is believed to be hiding in Shanghai. Stahl was last seen on Friday night. The French Consulate issued a subpoena on Sunday, and because they could not find him, they issued an arrest warrant yesterday (the 18th) afternoon. Stahl is a middle-aged man, not yet married, six feet three inches tall, and very strong. He has worked at Baolong Hospital for fifteen years and currently earns a monthly salary of 700 yuan. He owns property in Shanghai.

Reuters, Los Angeles, September 19: The Chinese girl, Wen Mali, 24 years old, arrived here last month and was arrested for possessing 48 pounds of heroin, worth $50,000 USD, in a hidden compartment, and charged with smuggling contraband. The woman is currently suffering from a severe case of influenza and gastroenteritis, so the case has been postponed. Several days after the incident, the woman attempted to escape to Europe on the German ship "Deutschland," but was re-arrested when the ship arrived in New York.

Dr. Ding Huikang Discusses Health Insurance Systems in Various Countries; China Health Care Society to Be Established Soon in Cooperation with the China Anti-Tuberculosis Association

Dr. Ding Huikang, a medical committee member of the China Anti-Tuberculosis Association, advocates for health insurance. On the evening of the 17th of this month, he hosted a reception for people from all walks of life at the New Asia Hotel. Li Dachao, Pan Gongzhan, Li Tingan, Yu Bohong, Yu Guang, Fang Zhizhi, Zhang Jing, Dong Douyan, Li Xiamen, and others inquired about Dr. Ding's plan. Last year, he promoted the establishment of tuberculosis prevention agencies in various places. Without a sound health insurance system, it would be difficult to achieve its goals. This system is divided into two categories. One is public, for civil servants, employees, and others, who contribute 4% to 6% of their income as health insurance fees, with designated doctors and hospitals providing protection. The other is private, for self-employed individuals, housewives, children, and others, who can join freely and request family doctor consultations. Currently, in Germany, more than 20 million people participate in health insurance, costing approximately 1.5 billion marks annually. In the United States, it costs approximately 3.6 billion USD, averaging 30 USD per person. Russia has 2.5 billion rubles in social insurance fees. Japan's tuberculosis prevention funding is 3 million yuan, and the cost of health care is more than 30 million yuan. Looking at the progress of their nations, it is all due to the popularity of health insurance, which can concentrate considerable economic resources and have complete medical construction to succeed. On the other hand, focusing only on treating individuals will hinder medical construction without any progress, leading to the decline of the nation and its international standing. The degradation of medicine is a sign of decline. Taking tuberculosis prevention as an example, patients in our country are currently unable to afford medical treatment. At the same time, due to the lack of regular treatment in hospitals and sanatoriums, it cannot be popularized. Most patients have no knowledge and only rely on internal medicine as the only remedy, leading to a widespread epidemic. To reverse this situation, the only solution is to popularize health insurance, so that people have access to normal medical protection and the possibility of early diagnosis. More importantly, it is necessary to have statistics on diseases and mutations, which is of great significance for public health and prevention. Recently, countries such as Italy and Switzerland have implemented compulsory lung disease insurance, which has achieved considerable results. The reasons for the decline in Germany's lung disease mortality rate are (1) the progress of public health, (2) the progress of eugenics, and (3) the progress of specialized medical methods. The greatest reason is the precise organization of public insurance institutions and the suitability of their implementation regulations for hygiene. When I was in Europe, I researched with experts there, and we all agreed that it is suitable for social needs and should use the simplest method, starting from one unit, to establish the "China Health Care Society" to achieve the goals of prevention and medical protection. However, the matter is significant, and I hope that leaders from all walks of life will provide guidance and promotion. Over the years, I have spent more than 350,000 yuan on various medical construction projects, and I will continue to do my best to serve society. It is said that the China Anti-Tuberculosis Council will discuss cooperation issues.

Beijing-Shanghai Railway to Prepare for Express Train; Multiple Test Runs to Determine Speed; Implementation Expected in November

After the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration laid double tracks on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, the train speed has gradually increased. In the current timetable, train No. 4 from Shanghai to Beijing and train No. 3 from Beijing to Shanghai take five hours and fifty minutes to complete the entire journey, making them the fastest passenger trains on the line. Now, the Ministry of Railways, to facilitate transportation on the line, has ordered the administration to prepare for the opening of an express train. The administration has ordered the Rolling Stock Department and the Engineering Department to determine the maximum possible speed, which is four hours and fifty minutes, and is drafting a timetable for approval by the ministry. Implementation is expected around November. The three departments are currently inspecting the tracks and locomotives to ensure that the project can be completed as scheduled.

Director Shen Inspects the Gaogiao Seawall in Shanghai; Creates a Budget to Submit to the Municipal Government for Appropriation; Earthen Seawalls Easily Eroded, to Be Replaced with Square Stones

The seawall in the Gaogiao area of Shanghai was damaged by the recent typhoon, with about five or six sections of the original earthen seawall being washed away by the waves and one or two sections breached. Shen Yi, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works, considered the seawall to be related to the safety of residents in the Pudong area of Shanghai, so he personally inspected the site with Xu Guansan, the director of the responsible section. In addition to sending more than 2,000 sacks to Gaogiao to block the breaches, the situation of the eroded earthen seawall was reported to the municipal government. The areas of the earthen seawall that need to be repaired have also been surveyed for budget preparation. A temporary budget will be submitted to the municipal government for appropriation and active repairs. According to Section Chief Xu, earthen seawalls are easily eroded, so the repairs will use stone as much as possible to ensure stability.

Public Concession Industrial Accidents in August

According to a report from the Factory Division of the Municipal Council, a total of 175 industrial and occupational accidents occurred in the Public Concession in August, resulting in five deaths and four injuries to women, but no deaths. The causes of the accidents were generally clear in 160 cases. Investigation and guidance on prevention and remedies were provided in 97 cases. In terms of the type of industry, the machinery and hardware manufacturing industry accounted for 46 cases, including one death; the building construction industry accounted for 20 cases, including two deaths; the textile industry accounted for 20 cases, with no deaths; the clothing manufacturing industry accounted for 11 cases, including two deaths; the food, beverage, and tobacco manufacturing industry accounted for 18 cases, with no deaths; and the transportation industry accounted for 17 cases, including one death. Analyzing the causes, 50 accidents were related to electrical machinery, including one death. No fewer than 20 injuries were caused by belts and gears. Six people were shocked by electricity, but none died. One person was injured and killed in an explosion. Six people were burned by molten metal, but none died. 29 people were injured by falling from heights, and two died. 27 people were injured by falling objects, but none were fatal.

Chen Mao Xian Abandons His Wife and Fails to Provide Support: Not Subsidizing Her Living Expenses or Welcoming Her Home

Chen Mao Xian, a local resident of Xue Nong Di in the city, is thirty-three years old. His father owns property there, and he comes from a wealthy family. Twelve years ago, he married Zhu Bao Zhen, who is now thirty-two years old. Initially, their relationship was good, and they had two sons. Later, due to marital discord, Zhu developed a mental illness after being emotionally distressed, with intermittent episodes lasting for seven or eight years. As a result, she has been living with her mother's family for two years. She previously sued her husband for failing to provide support, and the court ruled that he should pay 18 yuan per month for her medical and living expenses. However, this year, he stopped paying again and requested a divorce. Zhu argued that she has become disabled and is clearly being maliciously abandoned, with no means of self-support. Her mother's family sent her back to Chen's home, but his father refused to let her in. Furthermore, Chen recently sold land and received 19,000 yuan, so he is not incapable of providing support. Zhu also filed a complaint with the prosecutor. After reviewing the situation, the prosecutor determined that Chen Mao Xian was indeed guilty of abandonment and initiated a public prosecution. Yesterday, Judge Shao held a court session. Zhu explained the previous circumstances. The defendant, Chen Mao Xian, stated, "I used to work as a staff member at the Datong Dyeing and Weaving Factory, earning only 20 yuan per month, but she insisted on 18 yuan, so I had to embezzle from the accounts. At the end of last year, I was unable to repay the money and was dismissed. That is why I am unable to pay this year. The money from the land sale is managed by my parents, and I do not have access to it." At this point, Prosecutor Tang attended the court and argued that Chen was not subsidizing his wife's living expenses or allowing her to return home. This disabled and frail woman had no way to support herself and should be punished according to the law. The judge declared the arguments closed and scheduled the verdict to be announced at 10:00 AM on the 25th.

Lu Guo Qin and Ma Li's Adultery Dispute Verdict: Each Tells Their Side of the Story, Ma Li Found Not Guilty

Lu Guo Qin, a 21-year-old from Chongming, who works as a fruit shop clerk at Rong Tai at 1272 Route Lafayette (at the intersection of Route Ratard) in the French Concession, previously hired a lawyer to file a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Special No. 2 District Court. He accused Ma Li, a local woman residing at No. 46, Lane 550, Route Albert, of extortion and attempted fraud. He claimed that he was seduced by Ma Li, had a relationship with her, and lived with her for two months. Due to lack of money, he was kicked out. On August 20th and September 4th, she allegedly incited gangsters to extort 500 yuan from his store, demanding payment or threatening to kill him on the street. He requested an investigation. The court, concerned about potential nationality issues with the defendant's name, instructed Judge Zhang Zhao Zuo to first summon the plaintiff to investigate the case and then schedule a hearing, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, Judge Zhang summoned both parties to the Criminal Court No. 2 for questioning. According to the plaintiff, Lu Guo Qin, after living with the defendant, he gave her 120 yuan the first time and 125 yuan the second time. She quickly spent it and asked him for more. When he refused because he had no money, she sent gangsters to extort 500 yuan from him, threatening to kill him on the street if he didn't pay. The defendant, Ma Li, stated that the plaintiff's claims were completely false and fabricated. She denied having a relationship with him, stating that his behavior was despicable, and he associated with gangsters, wanting her to marry him. When she refused, he repeatedly harassed her, and she reported him to the police. She claimed he only earned five yuan a month and could not possibly have given her large sums of money. She accused him of falsely accusing her and damaging her reputation, and she planned to file a countersuit, hiring lawyer Xu Wu Fang for her defense. After hearing the testimony of Gu Fu Cai, a witness presented by the plaintiff, the court found the plaintiff's claims to be unfounded and considered the report made to the police, concluding that the plaintiff's statements were untruthful. After hearing the arguments of lawyer Er Zao, the court immediately announced the verdict: Ma Li was found not guilty. A case of adultery dispute thus came to an end.

First, the plaintiff Wang Xiu Ying stated that she was injured on the morning of the 9th due to a dispute with female worker Li A Si the day before regarding work. On the morning of the 9th, when she entered the factory to work, a police officer named Wang pushed her down, preventing her from working, and dragged her to the accounting room. Le Shun Ting and Shi Ji Fu shouted and beat her, stating that Li Ming Nai was responsible. Her body is still not fully recovered, and she is still taking medication. The other thirteen workers, including Kang Xiu Zhen, Zhang Hui Zhen, Zhang Xiu Ying, Sun A Ju, Zhang Feng Xian, Wang Chun Mei, Zhou Lin Bao, Lu Qin Xian, Chen Zhao Di, Zhu Xing Hua, Jin A Qin, Wei Xing Xian, and Ge Yu Shu, gave similar testimonies as Wang Xiu Ying. Li Ming Nai, Xia De Pei, Le Shun Ting, and Shi Ji Fu all denied committing the assault or inciting others to do so. The lawyers for both parties stated that the case was currently under mediation. The court reviewed the statements and ordered a postponement of the hearing to the 28th.

Yu Bin Appointed Director: Shanghai Catholic Action Association to Broadcast Celebration Tonight

Dr. Yu Bin, the National Director of the Catholic Action Association and Supervisor of Catholic Schools, was recently appointed by the Pope as the first Bishop of the Nanjing National Diocese. The appointment document has arrived, and the ordination ceremony will be held this morning (the 20th) at the Cathedral of the Savior in Beiping, with the Papal representative Archbishop Cai Ning officiating. The Shanghai Catholic Action Association, in addition to sending representatives to Beiping to offer congratulations and attend the ceremony, will broadcast a celebration program on the Shanghai Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications tonight from 8:00 PM to 9:00 PM. The radio frequency is 1300. The program is as follows: (1) Play the Archbishop's Processional March; (2) Report on the significance of the celebration; (3) Sing a Chinese celebration song; (4) Read Yu Bishop's biography; (5) Read congratulatory messages (Ma Xiangbo, Lu Bohong, etc.); (6) Sing a Latin celebration song; (7) Lecture on the history of the Nanjing Diocese; (8) String and piano ensemble; (9) Lecture on the current situation and prospects of the Nanjing Diocese; (10) Sing Vespers Hymn; (11) Report on the grand occasion of the ordination and the inauguration ceremony; (12) Play music for the completion of the ceremony. Military and political figures from Beiping, as well as diplomatic missions, have been invited to attend the ceremony, which promises to be a lively event. The new Bishop will arrive in Nanjing on October 4th to take office. Friends and Catholics in Nanjing are preparing a grand welcome ceremony.

Robbers Open Fire in Chuansha: Victim Injured and Hospitalized

At midnight the night before last, four robbers broke into the home of Ye Dao Lin, a 20-year-old resident of Li Duan Qi Jia in Chuansha County, Pudong. They robbed the family of more than ten yuan in national currency and a gold bracelet. When Ye Dao Lin attempted to call for help, the robbers became angry and shot him, hitting him in the abdomen. Ye Dao Lin collapsed to the ground, bleeding profusely. Ye's father was also seriously injured on the head by the robbers with their gun butts. Seeing that they had caused an incident, the robbers were about to flee with their loot when the local police station received a report and dispatched a large number of police detectives who arrested the robbers on the spot and brought them to the station for processing. The injured father and son were sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment.

Drug Den Cracked on Hua Ji Road: Three Sentenced, Two Released

Hua Detective Xu De Cheng of the police force cracked a den for smoking opium and heroin at No. 8, Lane 100, Hua Ji Road, at 8:30 PM the day before yesterday. Chen Yi Wu from Wenzhou, Yang Yan Qing, a woman Gao Chen Shi, and suspects Xu Yi Fu and Chen Da Ju were taken to the police station along with drug paraphernalia and a package of heroin. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Special District Court. The lawyer from the Bureau of Public Works, Zhang Shi Zhu, presented the case and requested an investigation. Detective Xu presented the evidence. After Judge Zhong Qing questioned the defendants, Gao Chen Shi was sentenced to one year and six months in prison, and Chen Yi Wu and Yang Yan Qing were each sentenced to six months in prison. All were sent to a drug rehabilitation hospital for a period of abstinence of no more than one month. The evidence was confiscated, and Xu Yi Fu and Chen Da Ju were released.

Chen Hui Zhang's Family's Private Prosecution Rejected

After rickshaw puller Chen Hui Zhang was beaten to death by a British sailor, his family reached a settlement with a compensation of 600 yuan. Afterward, the deceased's father, Chen Xi Zhu, and the deceased's wife, Chen Zang Shi, filed a private prosecution in the District Court against Xu Jie Li, the director of the West District Branch of the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association, Zhang Deng Ying, the general director of the Mutual Aid Association, and Cao A Da, accusing them of colluding with Maxi, the British head of the Bureau of Public Works' Traffic Department and chairman of the Mutual Aid Association, using fraudulent and coercive methods. Cao Wei allegedly posed as a relative of the deceased, forcing them to put their fingerprints on the agreement, selling out their grievance. They also claimed that 200 yuan was deducted from the compensation. They requested an investigation. After repeated hearings and the testimony of Maxi, the arguments were concluded. Yesterday, Judge Zhang announced the verdict, stating that Chen Xi Zhu's prosecution did not comply with the private prosecution procedure and rejected the private prosecution.

Armed Robbery at Xu Wen Yuan's Home: Two Robbers Sentenced

Robbers Bu Da Long and Gao Gui Sheng from Yancheng, along with Liu Hu Zi (who is still at large) and Shang Hong Fa (who was shot dead), broke into the home of Xu Wen Yuan, a Western doctor at No. 11, Lane 128, Route Ghisi, French Concession, armed with two Mauser pistols. When Xu's wife and servants shouted loudly, the robbers failed to search the home and fled. They encountered a French police patrol, and the Chinese and foreign police shot and killed Shang Hong Fa in front of the Yinse Automobile Company on Haig Road after the robbers opened fire. Liu escaped in the chaos, and Bu and Gao were captured and taken to the police station, along with the confiscated Mauser pistols. They were transferred to the Special No. 2 District Court, where the Police Department lawyer filed a public prosecution. Judge Zhang Zhao Zuo conducted the trial, as previously reported. The case has been concluded, and yesterday morning, Judge Zhang, presiding in the Criminal Court No. 1, sentenced Gao Gui Sheng to seven years in prison and Bu Da Long to five years in prison, with both being deprived of their civil rights for the duration of their sentences. The two Mauser pistols were confiscated. After the verdict, the two defendants were ordered to be detained in the detention center during the appeal period.

Fire at Zaojiadu Road: Originates from Yuan Yuan Tobacco and Paper Store

Yesterday morning at 8:30 AM, a fire broke out on the upper floor of Yuan Yuan Tobacco and Paper Store at No. 510 Zaojiadu Road in the South City. The patrol police reported to the fire department, which dispatched fire trucks to extinguish the fire. It took an hour to put out the fire, which destroyed the entire building. The cause of the fire was that the tenant, Ding Song He, had been cooking lunch, but had not completely extinguished the fire when he left home to work. Ding fled after the incident. The Ximen Branch of the police took Gao Jin Fu, the landlord from Pudong, into custody for questioning.

Doctor at Labor Hospital Accused of Negligence Causing Injury: Explanation

According to the Central News Agency, yesterday's newspaper reported that Tang Li Wen accused a doctor at the Labor Hospital of negligence causing injury. According to the hospital, on the 4th of this month, Tang Wang Shi's son, Da Shi Zi, went to the hospital for treatment. Dr. Zhang Xiu Yu of the hospital diagnosed the child with pinworms (not dysentery) and prescribed five packets of pinworm medicine. At 7:30 PM that evening, Tang Wang Shi brought her son Da Shi Zi back to the hospital, saying that when the child took the medicine, he spit it out on his neck because he didn't want to swallow it, and it caused an ulcer. After the hospital re-examined the child, they confirmed that the medicine on his body would not have caused such a reaction. They also mixed the medicine with warm water and tested it, and there were no other changes. (The newspaper reported that three packets were taken away, but this was likely a mistake, as one packet was used during the test.) It is also reported that the Public Security Bureau on Putuo Road has investigated the medicine and found no other abnormalities.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that Shandong and the Yellow River basin are clear, sometimes turning with strong south to west winds. The upper and middle reaches of the Yangtze River have light and variable winds. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River have northeast to southeast winds, with morning fog. The East China Sea and Taiwan will turn cloudy from overcast, with strong northeast breezes. Also, the highest temperature in this city within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 84.0 degrees, and the lowest was 61.2 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 82.4 degrees, and the lowest was 63.0 degrees.

Shanghai Open Doubles Tennis: Lin Baohua and Defu Win Championship; Carson Defeats Kolasha in Hard-Fought Singles

The finals of the Shanghai Open Tennis Doubles and Senior Singles were held yesterday afternoon at the French Chamber of Commerce. Lin Baohua and Defu cooperated perfectly and demonstrated excellent skills. Carson, unable to support himself, was defeated in straight sets. Carson's victory over Kolasha in the singles final was expected. The score was three to one. Details of the match follow:

Doubles Final

At 2:45 PM, Cass started strong, with long shots and short volleys, all executed with ease. Lin Baohua also displayed the demeanor of a famous player, with cross-court backhands often hitting the enemy's weak spots. The two sides were evenly matched, tying at 7-7. Squia repeatedly made unforced errors, and Carson was unable to save him. Lin and Defu took two consecutive games to win the first set 9-7. In the second set, Carson was cautious, and Squia showed renewed spirit. After each side won one game, Carson unleashed his divine power, with sharp and rapid cross-court shots, rendering the enemy helpless. He won two consecutive games. Lin Baohua quickly caught up, tying the score again. Cass won another game, but Lin's luck had arrived. His shots were directed at Squia's side, and Carson was unable to help. Lin and Defu won the second set 6-4 in one fell swoop. In the next set, at 2-2, Lin and Defu emerged as a surprise force, winning two consecutive games. Carson regained two games, but he was already powerless and ended the set 6-4.

Singles Final

Carson, barely recovered, immediately began the singles final against Kolasha. Kolasha was in high spirits and won three consecutive games. After that, Carson gradually calmed down and counterattacked at every opportunity, with precise shots. The two sides exchanged shots, unwilling to give in. At 7-7, Kolasha suddenly panicked, and Carson seized the opportunity to attack, winning the first set. Kolasha reorganized and gradually observed Carson's weaknesses in the second set, placing the ball unpredictably in front, behind, left, and right. Carson's strength gradually waned. Although he won three games, he lost 6-2. After that, although Kolasha fought with all his might, he was ultimately defeated due to inferior skills. Carson won two consecutive sets 6-4. Carson won the Shanghai Open Championship again this year.

New Autumn Football First Sound: Donghua Defeats Portugal Yesterday; Score 4-1, Halftime 2-1; Long Distance, Few Spectators, Only One Thousand

The Donghua Football Association, with the Western League approaching, played a friendly match against the strong Western team Portugal at the city sports field yesterday afternoon in order to reorganize its forces. This match was the first sound of the new season, but due to the long distance, the audience was not enthusiastic, totaling only about 1,200 to 1,300 people. As a result, Donghua defeated the Portuguese team 4-1, which shows that although Donghua's lineup is not yet fully stable, its strength is quite sharp. It is expected that when Sun Jia returns from his tour of Europe, the lineup will be even stronger. It is also heard that Donghua has invited the French Chamber of Commerce to play a friendly match at Yiyuan next Saturday (the 26th). The details of yesterday's match are as follows:

Wen Kui Headbutt

When the two sides took to the field, both teams wore white jerseys, so Donghua added a blue vest for identification. After the referee Shen Huichun gave the order, the Portuguese team started the attack, but it was blocked in the middle. Wan Xianghua was as brave as ever and intercepted the ball from the Portuguese team, rushing straight along the side. With a hook, Xu Wenkui caught up and headed the ball into the net, giving Donghua the first goal after only six minutes.

Portuguese Team Shows Its Skills

After several rounds, Donghua's Wenxiu hurriedly attacked the goal but was unsuccessful. Soon after, Remidi lost his footing while saving the ball. The Portuguese left-wing advanced, and Aquino fouled on the baseline. Zhuang Weixin took the free kick, but the kick was not far enough. The ball was obtained by Endaye, who passed it to the center forward. Luo Chai Liao kicked it horizontally and it flew in, losing one city and making it 1-1.

Yi Chen Makes Contribution

At 22 minutes, Dai Linjing again entered alone and headed the ball, but it did not go in. Feng Yunyou received it and shot again, but it was still unsuccessful. Repeatedly good opportunities were lost. In front of the Portuguese goal, there were many Donghua cavalrymen, causing great confusion. Yi Chen broke through from the middle and made a contribution, returning with a goal. Donghua won the first half 2-1.

Penalty Kick

The Portuguese team made major changes to its lineup. One attack was extremely dangerous, but it was safely passed. Soon after, Donghua launched a full-scale counterattack. The three generals Wan, Xu, and Li successively fired fiercely. Goalkeeper Lauren came out to resist the enemy. Because he did not notify the referee when changing positions, he was penalized with a penalty kick. Dai Linjing took the kick and hit the crossbar.

Completing the Great Achievement

After that, Dai's center forward and Portuguese center forward Luo Shi each made a fierce shot, but neither was effective. There were both dangers and ease, but there was no progress. In the last five minutes, Dai Linjing obtained a good opportunity 20 yards from the enemy's goal. He kicked the ball and it went into the net with a sound. The ball was low and fast, and Lauren dived to save it, but it went in under his waist. A few minutes later, when the whistle sounded, Donghua won the final victory 4-1.

General Situation of Sports Development in Qingdao: Two New Large Stadiums Built; Various Athlete Teams Organized

Qingdao Correspondent: Sports in Qingdao, through the efforts of the municipal authorities and the sincere cooperation of the sports community, is developing rapidly. The newly built First Park Stadium and the stadium at the Huiquan Racecourse have been completed one after another, and the organization of various representative teams in the city is also roughly on track. In the future, the development of Qingdao sports can be expected. The general situation of sports in this city is divided into two items: equipment and work, which are recorded separately below:

Sports Equipment: In addition to the large stadium built for the 17th North China Games, two new large stadiums have now been built. One is the Central Third Park Stadium, including fields for track and field, football, basketball, and equipment, specifically for the convenience of citizens who live far from the Huiquan Stadium to engage in sports. The other is a large stadium built in the Huiquan Racecourse, including one football field, small football field, rugby field, hockey field, croquet field, polo field, baseball field, and softball field, two basketball fields and volleyball fields, ten tennis courts, a heavy equipment field, a children's playground, and a track and field field for Chinese and foreign people to use for sports. The above two stadiums have been completed. The Third Park Stadium will be used by Lixian, Chongde, Wende Girls' Middle School, and Shangde Elementary School, which are located near the stadium, to hold joint sports meets in the stadium during this semester in order to commemorate it. The Huiquan Grand Stadium will also be officially opened on a regular basis. The development of sports in this city has always focused on popular development. Now that these two large stadiums have been completed, future progress is not difficult to predict. In addition, there is another project that is currently being planned and implemented, which will build a large swimming pool. Qingdao is located on the coast, and there are seven or eight bathing beaches along the coast. In recent years, due to the efforts to improve the facilities of the bathing beaches, citizens, regardless of men, women, old, or young, are very interested in seawater bathing, which is more popular than other sports. However, although there are many bathing beaches, it is difficult to accurately measure the results of formal competitions, and it is also inconvenient for athlete training. Now, the municipal authorities have decided to plan the construction of a swimming pool in response to the needs of the situation, so as to achieve the goal of completing sports facilities. The equipment of simple sports fields in various districts under the city is also built everywhere, with everything that should be available. With Qingdao being so large and sports facilities being complete, it is feared that it is rarely matched in other parts of the country.

Promotion Work: Qingdao's sports organizations are administratively the Sports Committee of the Education Bureau, and the Sports Promotion Association is for the public. In addition, there is a Sports Field Management Committee. The organizations are generally different, but the work is united and cooperatively divided. For four years, a good foundation has been laid for the promotion of sports in Qingdao. The cooperative spirit of the three committee members is very convenient for promoting work. Recently, in view of the tragic failure of our delegation at the World Games, it was decided to work hard and make Qingdao sports a considerable achievement. The important work is to organize various representative teams under the principle of popularity and sports, and to engage in training. The methods are: (1) In terms of schools, the Sports Committee will submit a request to the Education Bureau to order all secondary schools to first implement the organization of various school teams, with each team limited to ten people. The Sports Committee and the Sports Association will jointly formulate a confrontation program for circular matches in order to select elite city representatives; (2) In terms of amateurs, the Sports Promotion Association will earnestly organize the registration of various sports organizations and individuals in order to select outstanding talents and jointly organize the city representative team. Not only will there be a unified organization for participating in various major conferences in the future, but also when there are external competitions, the Sports Association will draw troops from various school teams or sports organizations to fight. This method can be said to be achieved in one fell swoop and has many benefits. In addition, in order to improve the standards of school sports, the Education Bureau will convene sports teachers from various schools to discuss methods and implement measurement to be used as a reference standard for achievements. In terms of martial arts, it is also actively promoting training centers, certifying martial arts teachers, and storing up teachers. The above are permanent implementation methods. As for temporary sports activities, in addition to various competitions that must be held at the sports field every week, the Chengzhang Cup Tennis Tournament and the compilation of the Qingdao Sports Yearbook have also been held recently.

Guo Youshou and Others from the Ministry of Education Inspect Education in Gansu; Gansu Province's Education Funding Increases Again This Year; Able to Handle Matters in Accordance with the Instructions of the Ministry of Education

(Lanzhou Airmail) Guo Youshou, Mei Yiqi, Dai Leren, and other experts from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund Board of Trustees for Northwest Education took off from Ningxia at 1:15 PM on September 9 and landed in Lanzhou at 3:00 PM. On the same day, they visited Chairman Yu and Director Tian to discuss the inspection schedule and began the inspection work the next morning (the 10th). On this day, they visited Gansu College and its affiliated high school and experimental primary school, Gansu Manufacturing Bureau and its affiliated apprentice school, Gansu Provincial Hospital, Gansu Provincial Hygiene Experimental Office, and Provincial Senior Midwifery School. The reporter learned that Guo and others originally planned to go to Tianshui, Pingliang, Wuwei, Zhangye, and other places to inspect, but due to inconvenient transportation and time constraints, they conducted more inspections of all schools and educational institutions in Lanzhou. However, of this Northwest inspection, only Qinghai Province has not been visited. The road between Lanzhou and Xining is mostly mountainous and usually feels rugged. Now it is the rainy season, making it even more difficult to travel. They changed their plans and chartered an aircraft from the Eurasia Company. It has now been properly contacted and is scheduled to open a special flight to Xining on the 19th (Saturday) specifically to send the inspection team members to go and pick them up again a week later. It is expected that before Guo and others fly to Qing on the 19th, they plan to spend the 17th and 18th drafting the Sui Ning West Province report and discussing the Gansu Province plan with Director Tian. After that, they will go to Qinghai for a week-long inspection and fly directly to Xi'an on the 26th. At that time, Guo will go to Wugong to inspect the National Northwest Agricultural and Forestry College and then return to Beijing to report to the Ministry of Education. Mei and Dai will return to Yenching University in Beiping to teach, and Li and Bai will continue to conduct inspections in Ningxia and Suiyuan provinces. The reporter asked Guo about his impression of the inspection of Gansu Province. Moreover, Gansu Province's education funding for the 25th year has increased again. Director Tian allocated 70,000 yuan to schools in other counties and hired more than 20 teachers from outside the province for major subjects (more than a dozen have arrived) to serve in secondary schools outside the provincial capital, which is a very good phenomenon.

Jiangsu Province Implements Preliminary Education Guidance Zone System

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education issued an order to the education bureaus of various counties, stating that in order to improve elementary education in various counties, the department previously established elementary education instructors within the affiliated primary schools of various normal school districts. They were responsible for actively guiding the improvement of primary schools in their respective districts. After years of guidance, gradual progress has been made. However, due to the vastness of the area and the large number of schools, although widespread supervision has been implemented, specialized inspection is still insufficient, hindering the rapid promotion of improvement. As the new year begins, it has been decided to designate 20 to 30 primary schools in each normal school district as elementary education guidance zones, actively guiding their improvement. The achievements of these improvements will serve as models for other schools, and the methods adopted for guidance will serve as examples for inspectors. A nine-article outline of the "Jiangsu Province Trial Implementation of the Elementary Education Guidance Zone System" has been specially formulated. In addition to separate orders, the complete outline is urgently issued for the bureau chief to take note of. Each zone should have two elementary education instructors, one responsible for routine guidance matters, residing in the guidance zone, and the other responsible for general inspection work, allocated by the provincial supervisor of each district. This is for your information. Attached below is the "Jiangsu Province Trial Implementation of the Elementary Education Guidance Zone System" outline:

Outline of the Jiangsu Province Trial Implementation of the Elementary Education Guidance Zone System

Article 1: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education formulates this outline for the trial implementation of the elementary education guidance zone system, to serve as a model for education personnel in various counties. Article 2: The Department of Education designates 20 to 30 primary schools in each normal school district of the province as elementary education guidance zones. Article 3: Each guidance zone should establish a guidance committee composed of the provincial supervisor inspecting the local education in the normal school district, the principal of the district's normal school, the principal of the affiliated primary school, the elementary education instructor, and the local education chief (or section chief), the county supervisor, and one education committee member. The provincial supervisor serves as the chairman. The committee convenes meetings twice each semester to discuss and decide on the main points of guidance and other important matters for each zone. Article 4: The elementary education instructor serving as the guidance committee member in each guidance zone serves as the guide. The guide should reside in the zone and visit each school in the zone at least twice a month, providing active guidance separately and assessing the results of their improvement. A guidance meeting should be held once a month to guide and jointly discuss improvement methods. When necessary, demonstration teaching, reciprocal observation and critique, and exhibition competitions should be held to facilitate mutual learning. Article 5: Each school in the guidance zone should accept the guidance of the guide and strive for improvement. If anyone fails to follow the guidance, the guide may correct it at any time or consult with the provincial supervisor for handling. Article 6: Existing inspectors in the locality of the guidance zone should be guided by the guide when inspecting the zone. Any administrative sanctions should be agreed upon with the guide. Article 7: The guide should submit diagnostic inspections, guidance plans, and progress reports to the provincial supervisor periodically, who will then submit them to the Department of Education for review and selective publication, for reference by education administrative personnel and primary school teachers in various counties. Article 8: The operating expenses of each guidance zone are paid from the business expenses of the affiliated primary school in each normal school district. Article 9: This method is promulgated and implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education.
