Jiangsu Province Air Defense Exhibition Scheduled to Open

To be held at the Provincial People's Education Center starting on the 23rd. A discussion was held with principals of major middle schools and universities the other day to discuss organizing school propaganda teams and other cases.

(Zhenjiang Correspondence) The Jiangsu Provincial Capital Air Defense Exhibition has been scheduled to open on the 23rd. Therefore, preparations are being actively made in haste. Various models are extremely realistic, and small arms are also something that the general public has never seen before. The arrangements have already begun to be completed yesterday. The details are recorded below:

Called Principals' Talk

The Military Affairs Commission's Jiangsu Provincial Air Defense Exhibition called a talk with principals of middle schools and vocational schools, which was held yesterday morning at 10:00 AM in the reception room of the Jiangsu Provincial Party Headquarters. The attendees included Gu Zhengqi from Chongshi Girls' Middle School, Li Zongwei from the Provincial Obstetrics School, Ouyang Ge from the Dianlei School, Hu Ding'an from the Medical Administration College, Zhang Zhenyu from the Southeast Vocational School, Qu Deming from the Jiangsu Provincial Capital Compulsory Literacy Committee, Shen Pingzhou from the Private Zhenzhong School, Cao Chu from the Zhen Normal School, Fadu from the Vocational School, Sheng Lanqiu from the Supplementary School, and Zhang Manyu, Liang Zhiping, Zhou Diya, Lei Cheng, and Lin Yinbai from the Air Defense Association. Zhou Diya chaired the meeting, and Wu Xiangzhi recorded the minutes. The chairman reported the significance of the air defense exhibition, and the discussion items were: 1. How should the propaganda teams of each school be reorganized? It was decided that each school should have 50 people, with one chief captain, five captains (ten people per team, half male and half female), and each team should be divided into two groups with two group leaders. 2. The organizational chart of the propagandists of each school should be sent to the meeting within a time limit. It was decided that it should be sent to the propaganda group of the Air Defense Exhibition at the People's Education Center before 5:00 PM on the 19th. 3. The date of training for the propagandists. It was decided that they should arrive at the National Grand Theater before 8:00 AM on the 22nd to watch the air defense film. After the film ends at 9:30 AM, the theater will organize the teams to go to the auditorium of the Provincial Party Headquarters for centralized training and distribute propaganda materials. At 3:00 PM in the afternoon, the chief captains of each school will lead the teams to visit the Air Defense Exhibition at the People's Education Center. 4. The departure date of the propaganda team. It was decided that the propaganda period would be from the 23rd to the closing day of the defense exhibition on the 27th (a total of five days). They would depart at 8:00 AM to 11:00 AM and 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM each day to carry out propaganda separately. 5. How should the propaganda method be determined? It was decided that (1) door-to-door propaganda, (2) general lectures, and (3) distribution of leaflets and pamphlets would be used.

Student Air Defense Speech Contest

The Military Affairs Commission's Jiangsu Provincial Capital Air Defense Exhibition Student Air Defense Speech Contest Method, the original text is as follows: 1. The Provincial Capital Primary and Secondary School Student Air Defense Speech Contest will be held in accordance with the provisions of this method. 2. Participants in the competition are limited to students from public and private specialized schools and primary and secondary schools in the provincial capital. Each specialized school and middle school will select two representatives to participate, and each primary school will select one person. 3. The competition is divided into two groups: specialized school and middle school group and primary school group. 4. The competition time is scheduled for September 25th, starting at 8:00 AM for the primary school group and 2:00 PM in the afternoon for the middle school group. 5. The competition venue is the auditorium of the Jiangsu Provincial Party Headquarters. 6. The names and manuscripts of the student representatives participating in the competition should be submitted to the Propaganda Group of the Jiangsu Provincial Air Defense Exhibition before September 23. 7. Participants in the competition must draw lots before the speech to determine the order and speak in sequence. 8. The speaking time for each person is stipulated as follows: The primary school group should not exceed 5 minutes. If the time is exceeded, the bell will ring to stop the speech. The specialized school and middle school group should not exceed 8 minutes. The bell will ring to notify them at 7 minutes, and the bell should ring at 8 minutes, and the speech should be stopped immediately. Points will be deducted for exceeding the time. 9. Competition evaluation standards: 1. Content 42%, Language 33%, Posture 30%. 10. The number of winners in each group will be announced after the judges' meeting. 11. Prizes will be given to the winners of the competition. 12. This method will be formulated, promulgated and implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Capital Air Defense Exhibition. (Attached) The military and police group applies the middle school group method, and the people's school applies the primary school group method.

Overview of Japanese Schools in Shanghai (I)

— Hu Zuyin

Japanese residents in Shanghai have established four Japanese primary schools and three middle schools in Shanghai, with a total of 3,767 students. This article will provide a brief introduction to the various facilities of Japanese primary and middle schools. The author is grateful to Mr. Kanno Masaburo, the head of the Japanese Residents' Group, and Mr. Hosoki Nobuo, the secretary, for providing various materials. I would also like to thank Mr. Ishizawa, the principal of the Middle Japanese Normal Primary School, and Mr. Mizuguchi Minjiro, the principal of the Japanese Girls' High School, for giving me a picture of each school building. I also thank my colleague Mr. Chu Yingrui for determining the transliteration of names.

1. History of School Establishment

Japanese residents have been running schools in Shanghai for 51 years. In 1885, a monk belonging to the Higashi Honganji Temple independently founded a Japanese school to educate Japanese children in Shanghai. This school is the origin of the current Japanese primary school; at that time, less than 20 children were enrolled, and the curriculum in the school was limited to reading, arithmetic, and writing.

In 1900, the school was changed to public and renamed Kaido Primary School; the number of students increased to about 50. Five years later, the school was taken over by a community organized by Japanese residents. In 1907, the Shanghai Japanese Residents' Group was officially established, and the group accepted the responsibility of running Japanese schools; at this time, the number of students had increased to about 200.

In recent years, the number of Japanese residents in Shanghai has gradually increased; Japanese schools have also been added accordingly. New schools have been established in the east, west, and central districts of the city. There are now a total of seven Japanese schools with a total of 3,767 students. These schools are all managed by the Shanghai Japanese Residents' Group and supervised by the Japanese Consul General in Shanghai. The names, addresses, and establishment dates of the Japanese schools are listed as follows:

Survey Table of Names, Addresses, and Establishment Dates of Japanese Schools in Shanghai

Japanese residents in various places in Shanghai send their children to Japanese schools, so the number of students in each school is very large. The statistics of the number of male and female students in each school are recorded below:

Statistics Table of the Number of Male and Female Students in Japanese Schools in Shanghai (Statistics for 1935)

Note: Among the number of students in the above schools, there are two Chinese female students and one male student.

Securities: The Government Bond Market Was Quiet as Usual, Each Bond Was Only Slightly Down by 0.15 to 0.3

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange had another accident at Nanfengtai, but the people's hearts were still very stable, and the surface did not cause any waves. In the past, when the number of deposits was huge, it would have caused a huge disturbance. At present, the deposits are very different from the past, so the storm is difficult to be big, and the water waves are not. If no huge new transactions are added, it may not be easy to cause a big drop. Yesterday's... Therefore, the market was able to maintain... The second round immediately returned to one-fifth of a corner. The firmness of the table can be seen. After the afternoon opening, there was a slight... The opening fell by another small one-fifth of a corner, and the closing fell by another small one-fifth of a corner. Most of the 46 and 52 series were sold, 11 series were slightly bought, and the rest were just retail transactions. The future rise and fall will change with the evolution of the situation. The market price result was a small decrease of 0.15 to 0.25, and the total turnover was 5,185,000 yuan. The results of the rise and fall are compared in the table on the left. North-South Goods: Raw Sun-Dried Meat Market Fluctuates Slightly

Raw Sun-Dried Meat: Although the recent arrivals haven't been overwhelmingly abundant, various dealers haven't cleared their stocks smoothly. Consequently, the market remains soft, trending downwards. Yesterday, it was heard that several dozen boxes were released from major dealers, with prices for both Shima and Tong'an dropping nearly a dollar. However, according to reports from Zhangzhou, while the prices for raw meat materials are softening, they are still meeting the demand in Shanghai.

Yarn and Cotton

Yarn Flower Speculation, Stagnant Outlet for Arbitrage Yarn, Weak Trend in Marked Yarn, Especially Severe Decline in Current Month

The yarn market is trending downwards, with a weak outlook. This is due to the lackluster performance of overseas yarn and cotton. With the September settlement period approaching, there are several thousand bales of arbitrage yarn. This cotton yarn is particularly sluggish, unwelcome, and the unfavorable environment has pushed market prices lower.

Slack Market in Marked Yarn

The opening of the marked yarn market showed a uniform decline across all months. News of a clash between Japanese and Chinese troops in Fengtai has caused panic, leading to a lack of buying interest and a step-by-step decline in the market, showing a slack trend. According to some, there are still several thousand bales of old arbitrage chips in the current month. This cotton yarn is sluggish and unwelcome, causing the market to worsen. Changfeng, Run Kang, Yong Da, Xie Cheng, Rui Da, and others sold slightly, while Geng Feng, Yi Chang, Tai Chang, and Fu Kang slightly increased their long positions. Both long and short positions saw minimal activity. As a result, all months fell by one, two, and three jiao compared to the previous day's closing price. The afternoon opening saw a significant drop in the current month's market, due to a lack of buyers, and a two yuan drop in near-month third-grade yarn. However, the far months were tighter, with the second and third sessions remaining weak. As a result, the current month fell by six jiao compared to the morning closing price, and the far months rose by two and a half jiao. Sales included 1,150 bales from Da Feng, 850 bales from Rui Da, 800 bales from Sen Kang, 2,900 bales from Changfeng, 2,450 bales from Run Kang, 800 bales from Xie Cheng, 800 bales from Yong Da, and 850 bales from Wang Tai Yu. Purchases included 650 bales from Yu Da, 600 bales from Ji Feng, 700 bales from Tai Yu, 1,350 bales from Geng Feng, 800 bales from Tai Chang, 1,400 bales from Yi Chang, 1,300 bales from Xin Cheng, 600 bales from Shun Ji, and 600 bales from Sheng Yuan. The day's high and low prices are listed below:

Hope for Bumper Crop of New Cotton, Resurgence of Falling Cotton Prices

The cotton market is experiencing a resurgence of falling prices, with a mediocre market sentiment. The US cotton market is lackluster, and with clear weather, there is hope for a plentiful supply of new cotton from various sources. Ningbo merchants have resumed speculative selling, and Changhe is also selling, causing a sudden relaxation in the market. However, some cotton merchants are optimistic and are buying in. In general, this year's harvest is bountiful, and there are sellers eager to unload when prices rise.

Sudden Large-Scale Speculative Selling by Ningbo Merchants

The marked cotton market opened with fluctuations of one pound sterling for US cotton, a rise of one rupee for Indian cotton, and a fall of two jiao and three fen for Osaka second-grade cotton. The local weather is clear, and the new cotton is gradually flooding the market. Ningbo merchants have suddenly engaged in large-scale speculative selling, with a substantial volume, putting pressure on the market. The market is declining step by step, with Yuan Yu Chang and Changfeng Fu Kang showing strong selling intentions. However, Da Fu, Da Feng, Yuan Da, Jin Chang, Wang Tai Yu, Da Chang, Xin Cheng, and others are covering short positions and increasing their long positions simultaneously. As a result, all months fell by two, three, four, and five jiao compared to the previous day's closing price. The afternoon opening saw some covering, with a slight rebound of one jiao to one and a half jiao. However, after one session, it was reported that 11,000 bales of Yao cotton would arrive tomorrow, and the factory's appetite was not as strong as the previous day, causing the market sentiment to weaken again. As a result, all months rose or fell by nine fen compared to the morning closing price. Sales included 2,800 dan from Shen Ji, 1,500 dan from Da Fu, 4,600 dan from Heng Feng, 1,000 dan from Xing Chang, 1,600 dan from Hua Feng, 1,700 dan from Wang Tai Xing, 4,000 dan from Chang Yu, 5,600 dan from Run Kang, 1,200 dan from Jing Hua, 1,900 dan from Jin Kang, 1,600 dan from Yuan Xing Chang, 3,000 dan from Hua Kang, 1,200 dan from Da Chang, 7,300 dan from Chang He, and 2,700 dan from Ming Hua. Purchases included 1,800 dan from Ji Feng, 1,200 dan from Da Feng, 2,200 dan from Yuan Da, 3,200 dan from Geng Feng, 3,900 dan from Tai Chang, 6,200 dan from Xin Cheng, 2,300 dan from He Xing, and 4,200 dan from Shen Chang. Spot cotton consumption is mediocre, with factory demand lower than the previous day. The source is 4,850 bales of Yao cotton, with an asking price of 34 yuan and 6 jiao, down 2 jiao from yesterday. Common cotton is 890 bales, with an asking price of 45 yuan.

US Cotton Region Unaffected by Hurricane

The cotton market opened with positive news from Liverpool. Traders in Liverpool and the Far East were buying, pushing prices up by four to five pound sterling across all months. The western cotton region continued to experience rain, while local traders and New Orleans were selling. Southern speculative selling increased, causing market prices to soften. Spot cotton prices remained firm, with active demand. Hester estimated this week's factory usage at 204,000 bales, and Liverpool's inventory at 230,000 bales. It was reported that the eastern cotton region was unaffected by the hurricane. The closing was stable, with spot prices unchanged and futures falling by one pound sterling to rising by two pound sterling. British spot cotton rose by two points, and futures rose by one point. Indian cotton initially rose due to buying by futures traders and speculators, but later fell due to selling by spot traders. Ping Guo Er rose by 1.25 rupees, and Aomu La and Bai Luo Xi rose by one rupee. The original telegram is listed below (dated 18th):

Simultaneous Drop in Third-Grade Yarn and Cotton

According to a telegram from Osaka on the 19th, second-grade cotton futures fell by 2 jiao to 1 yuan, with near-month contracts at 214 yuan and 6 jiao, and far-month contracts at 102 yuan and 6 jiao. Yarn futures fell by 5 fen to 7 jiao, with near-month contracts at 264 yuan, 5 jiao and 5 fen, and far-month contracts at 64 yuan and 3 jiao.

Grain, Sluggish Trading in Flour Futures

Yesterday's flour market was quiet and peaceful throughout the day. After the morning session, news of overseas wheat reported that Chicago wheat was down a little, Canadian wheat down five jiao, and Liverpool wheat down one and a half pence. Overseas markets showed mixed fluctuations with no major trend. Initially, factories slightly bought back near-month contracts and covered floating short positions, making the market slightly stable. However, as yarn and cotton prices fell, market sentiment was slightly affected, and both near and far-month contracts saw dispersed selling. The afternoon session showed weakness, but trading was sluggish with no intense competition, fluctuating only by around half a fen. In total, the day's results showed September 12 unchanged, November up half a fen, January up seven and a half li, and October and February each up two and a half li.

Wheat Market Weak

Yesterday's wheat futures market saw overseas wheat prices fluctuating after the morning opening, with both buying and selling interest being weak. Near and far-month prices fluctuated by only one or two fen. However, when the flour market rebounded in the afternoon, buying interest weakened, and both near and far-month contracts fell by two or three fen. However, selling pressure was not strong, so weakness was not pronounced, and the situation remained peaceful. Compared to the previous day's closing price, September was down one fen, October and February were down three fen each, December was down two fen, and November and January were down four fen each. The spot wheat market was stable, with Shandong Yingzhou Shaheji Zhangbaling wheat ranging from 5.08 yuan to 5.04 yuan. Zhengyangguan wheat was 5 yuan, and Anqing wheat was 4.8 jiao. A total of 3,000 bales were purchased in the morning session, with Shen Da purchasing 800 bales.

River Rice Outlets Still Good

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the sources of various gangs were even scarcer, with only shipments from around the 10th, totaling nearly 2,000 shi. Therefore, the market for new sharp-pointed rice was even more brisk, with prices increasing by a fraction of an inch. New Yangjian rice also increased slightly. New Japonica rice increased slightly, but thick early japonica rice remained stable due to flat retail sales. Thin rice, handled by the Qingdao gang at over 400 packages, saw no ups or downs in price, remaining roughly the same.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, various goods from He Xia arrived around the 30th. Sales of various types in the market were still active. High-quality broken japonica rice prices were flat, while medium and lower-quality rice increased by a few fen to about one jiao. Old Yangjian rice was scarce and stable, while new Yangjian rice was slightly tight. The price of new port group customer rice increased by about one jiao. The price of new western japonica rice was tight, while new eastern japonica rice saw little rise or fall.

Page 18

Guangdong Sales of Guest Rice Very Brisk

Yesterday, guest indica rice arrivals and sales were both brisk, and the market atmosphere was very good. New arrivals in the past two days totaled about 10,000 bags. However, sales in Guangdong were very active, and some were directly transported for sale, so the market was not significantly affected by the surge in new arrivals. The new arrivals in the past few days were mainly machine-milled rice, while there were fewer arrivals of brown rice, which was suitable for the Guangdong gang's brisk handling. The price rose sharply by six or seven fen to over one jiao. Other machine-milled rice prices were generally flat. The total market opening included 4,510 bags of Hunan rice, 5,110 bags of Jiangxi rice, 1,100 bags of brown rice from Hankou and Shashi, and 85 bags of Taiwan indica rice, which were distributed by various gangs from Guangdong, Shantou, Ningbo, Xiamen, and local areas.

Foreign Bank Sesame Arrivals in Succession

Foreign bank sesame prices were previously 12 yuan, reportedly up to 11 yuan and 9 jiao, with 600 deals. Yesterday, the market first traded at 11 yuan and 9 jiao, then 11 yuan and 9 jiao and a half fen, with 300 tons traded. The market tightened later due to continued buying, but no deals were opened. The future direction is still uncertain, and prices largely follow the market's fluctuations. Because new sources from various places are continuously arriving, market sentiment is little excited by foreign bank sales. The Dongyang gang handled over 1,000 bags from Shashi, the Quanzhou gang handled 105 bags of Haozhou sesame, and the rest were small, scattered amounts. Yamamoto Street and others handled over 400 bags.

Silk and Tea, Silk Sales Both Domestic and Foreign Subside Again

Yesterday, overseas silk markets fell slightly again (New York recent contracts down 1 fen, far contracts down 1.5 fen, Yokohama spot and futures contracts each down 8 yuan). This led to a renewed lull in Shanghai silk markets, except for continued sales by Xinfu Lianna. Users of silk, hearing that this autumn's cocoon crop will only be 70% of normal, most silk merchants are maintaining a bullish price outlook and are unwilling to sell. The domestic sales situation is therefore also stagnant. In the evening, Yokohama far-month contracts rebounded and silk trading on the New York Stock Exchange was not quiet (volume was 1,060 bales), so next week's silk market seems likely to gradually stabilize or possibly rally.

Possibility of Full Sale of Red Tea

Since the Anhui-Jiangxi Red Tea Sales Office proposed a plan to completely sell the 7,000+ remaining cases of red tea on the market, foreign firms such as Xiehe, Yihua, and Jixiang, as well as Wang Yutai Tea Shop, have paid close attention. Overall, Wang Yutai's ability to sell and adapt makes their buying power stronger. It is heard that tea merchants from Qifu to will convene a meeting today to discuss countermeasures and a decision may be made within days.

Green Tea Market Quiet This Week

According to a report from the Tea House Association, the green tea market has been quiet this week. Sales have been brisk since the beginning of the season due to stable prices, so exports are more than double those of the same period last year. In recent weeks, arrivals of tea have been scarce, and inventories are low. Most of the high-quality tea has already been sold, causing foreign orders to question the prices of the remaining tea, and buyers need to consider this. Therefore, the market is temporarily quiet, with only scattered transactions. This week, Baotou Hangjin made the most purchases, totaling 1,030 boxes. Other purchases included only 280 boxes of Chouzhen and 370 boxes of Xiaozhenmei. Pingshui tea, large lots and other types of tea have also been out of the market for a long time. Discussions are underway with foreign firms, and it is hoped that activity will increase next week.

Piece Goods, Sales of Western-Style Lining Fabric Also Brisk

With autumn sales in full swing for woollen fabrics, accessories for Western-style clothing, such as sleeve linings and Western-style lining fabrics, are being purchased in large quantities by Western-style clothing stores in this street. Prices are also firm. The trend for printed Western-style fabrics and mabu sleeve linings is particularly good. The original cloth of printed striped Western-style fabrics produced by Guohua and sold by Jinyuan is selling for 5 jiao 5 fen per full piece. Hongsheng woven striped Western-style fabrics are selling for 5 jiao 3 fen. The mabu sleeve linings produced by Qinhua and sold by Dachangyu are selling for 5 jiao 5 fen per yard of the original cloth. Daohua first-class is 7 jiao, second-class is 6 jiao. Black carbon lining and Jiangshan lining, as well as Faxi lining, are also selling well. Yesterday, Aier 277 Western-style goods were all priced at 6 jiao and 5 fen, Dongfang goods at 4 jiao and 2 fen, Renyu at 4 jiao, and Guohua Hongsheng at 3 jiao and 9 fen. Hongsheng first-class black carbon lining is selling for 1 yuan and 4 jiao, second-class is 1 yuan and 2 jiao and a half. Ningbo Jiangshan 9-inch horsehair lining is 2 jiao.

Sugar Market, Refined Green and Sliced Green Both Rise Continuously

Yesterday's sugar market showed a firm trend with little change. The association's price list showed that spot second-grade coarse sugar white and re-exported goods were all priced at the original price. Dongbai only saw a 5-fen rise in the price of No. 8 re-exported goods, to 6 yuan and 2 jiao, with the rest as before. Local cotton white was held at the original price. There were Chaozhou gang openings on the numbered plate, with Zuihe Ti Ning 51 at 15 yuan, an increase of 4.5 jiao. There were no continued openings for high-quality cotton red. Sixty more packages of second-grade Zhuang were sold, with lower-quality goods. Furthermore, the Guangxi gang opened 104 boxes of Beihai sliced green at 10 yuan and 2 jiao, an increase of one jiao.

Upon Whose Shoulders Does the Future Glory Rest?

— Zhai Fu

The "September 18th" National Humiliation Memorial has been forgotten again!

We should deeply reflect: National humiliation is not created overnight; nor can it be washed away in a single day. Just look at people's bodies. A weak body doesn't become weak in a day or two. A strong body isn't built in a day or two either.

The nation's weakness is not the fault of one or two people; it is the cumulative fault of the entire nation over a hundred years. To wash away national humiliation cannot be accomplished by the power of one or two people now or in the future. It requires the joint struggle of the entire nation for ten, twenty, even a hundred years, from now until the future, to be effective.

Consider our representatives who returned from the World Games with a "zero score." We consider this a great regret in national honor. But this regret is not because our athletes were unwilling to work hard at the Olympics. It is fundamentally due to the fact that our "physical strength is inferior to others!" Therefore, in various competitions, we can often compete at the beginning, but then we fail.

Someone said, "To win glory in future World Games, we must start by cultivating the physical fitness of the people: it will take at least fifteen years to see results." Therefore, the future national honor rests on the shoulders of the children of today. If students in elementary schools today are well-trained physically, they will certainly not return with a "zero score" from the World Games fifteen years later.

It is not only sports that are like this. Our country needs talents in many fields. In addition to everyone needing to train their bodies, children must also diligently hone themselves in any area they are naturally drawn to!

Preparation

— Wan Wen

In life, whether adult or child, male or female, for every day we live, there is work to be done. No matter the size of the task, preparation is necessary before it can be carried out.

Many small but beneficial things in the world are overlooked and forgotten, which is very regrettable. If they could be utilized, much benefit could be gained. Children! You might as well try preparing and see if I am right.

First, let me compare the results of preparation and non-preparation. Take exams at school, for example. If you review your books before the exam in preparation, you won't feel difficulty during the exam because it's all familiar material. Even if you don't know one or two questions, it doesn't matter. When the scores are announced, your grades will definitely be excellent, or at least your ranking won't be too low. If you don't review your books before the exam in preparation and rely only on what you've heard and seen on weekdays, your mind will not be able to remember many questions. During the exam, you will definitely feel difficulty, and cheating will occur. If you are caught by the teacher, not only will your grades be poor, but you will also lose your integrity. Children probably have this experience. I hope you will act in a good way, which is to prepare beforehand.

However, preparation cannot be perfunctory in a short time. You must prepare fully until you are completely proficient. Only such preparation can achieve great results, which cannot be compared to the results of short-term preparation.

Children! What are you preparing for? Your current studies are preparing you to shoulder the important responsibilities of the country in the future. As your age increases, your responsibilities become greater, and preparation becomes more important. Those who study medicine prepare to serve in the medical field; those who study teacher training prepare to serve in the educational field; those who study aviation prepare to strengthen the country's defense. Know that the foundation of preparation is laid in your childhood.

Small Game

— Lu Changfan

Children, do you have galvanized iron downspouts under your eaves? If you do, when the downspout is slightly broken (make sure it's not too broken), you can use it to make a very interesting toy.

The shape of this thing must be like the one in the first picture. After making it into this shape, place a mirror at point A in the first picture, and another mirror at point B. The two mirrors should face each other. After placing the two mirrors, use something like a cigarette can lid, cut a round hole in the middle, and install it at point C. Close one of your eyes and look into the tube, and you will see many scenes outside the tube.

National Hero Zu Ti

— Zeng

Zu Ti was a person of the Jin Dynasty. From childhood, he had great ambitions and had an excellent relationship with his friend Liu Kun. They often slept in the same bed. One night, Zu Ti woke up in the middle of the night. In a haze, he suddenly heard the sound of a rooster crowing. It crowed loudly again and again. He quickly woke Liu Kun and said, "It's almost dawn. Listen, how impassioned the rooster's crow is!" After Liu Kun heard him, he hurriedly got up, and the two of them took down the precious swords on the wall and danced together for a while.

Soon after, the Five Barbarians caused chaos in China, and the Jin Dynasty moved south. The northern part of our country was all under the influence of the barbarian forces. Fortunately, Zu Ti led a large army to attack north. When he crossed the river, he struck the oar, pointed at the river water, and swore in a very tragic way: "If Zu Ti cannot pacify the Central Plains, I will never cross this river again." His will was very firm. Later, he defeated the barbarians and made them flee in defeat, and the area south of the Yellow River was completely recovered.

Children: Work hard! I hope that you will become national heroes like Zu Ti and clean up the current mess in our country!

Physical Science Knowledge

Why Does the Body Feel Cold After Bathing?

— He Zixiang

Children: When the weather is hot or you are working hard, the sweat glands on our body secrete a kind of liquid, which is sweat. After sweating, you should bathe; otherwise, it will have a bad influence on your body.

Children! When you come out of the bath, you must have the feeling and question, "Why does my body feel cold?"

When you come out of the bath, there are water droplets attached to your body. The water droplets absorb heat and vaporize, which takes heat from our bodies; so our bodies feel cold after bathing.

Why is it easier to swim when you inhale more air?

Children: Have you learned to swim during the summer vacation? Swimming is a very good exercise that develops physical fitness, increases lung capacity, and has the effect of emergency rescue, so it is necessary and valuable to learn.

Anyone who can swim has this concept: "When swimming, inhaling a large amount of air saves effort." Why does it save effort? Children! I will tell you:

When we inhale a large amount of air while swimming, the lungs expand, and the volume of the whole body also increases, so the buoyancy is greater. And the weight of the inhaled air is very small: so it feels easier when swimming.

Children! When you learn to swim, you can prove that this is true.

Love the Zoo Carp in the Lotus Pond

— Dong Xun

The water lilies in the pond are blooming!

White flowers,

Green round leaves,

How beautiful!

And those carp,

Green, black, red, orange;

Swimming around,

Are the masters of the lotus pond!

Younger brother and sister came to the lotus pond,

The fish float to the surface to welcome them,

They throw bran cakes into the water,

Let them dance and chase after them,

Opening their mouths to swallow with a "zhe bo, zhe bo" sound,

The cakes get wet and gradually soften and sink,

The carp follow the cakes and dive to the bottom of the water,

But when the cakes are thrown again, they float to the surface again.

The younger sister said:

"Cake after cake is thrown, one after another is tossed,

Fish, fish, you must be careful!

Fortunately, we are not fishermen,

Otherwise, we would have fished you into the basket early and taken you home to cook!"

The fish swim as if to say:

"The people in the world are all bad-hearted,

Only younger brother and sister are good people,

We only eat your small bran cakes,

We don't taste other people's hooked cakes!"

What Does the Northeast Four Provinces Have?

— Jun Peng

The tragic "September 18th" Memorial Day has passed in an instant. This year is the fifth anniversary. But in your sorrow, have you ever thought about why Japan wants to seize it? It is because the Northeast Four Provinces are rich in products and are the lifeline of our country. So, "What does the Northeast Four Provinces have?" Here I will briefly write some of them below:

What are the four provinces of the Northeast? Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe. Among the four provinces, Heilongjiang has the largest area, and Rehe has the smallest. Liaoning Province has an area of 850,000 square miles, and about 13.34 million residents. The Han ethnic group is the largest, followed by the Manchu and Mongolian ethnic groups. Jilin Province has an area of 880,000 square miles, and less than 6 million residents. Heilongjiang Province has an area of 1,780,000 square miles, and a population of only 5 million. Rehe Province has an area of 580,000 square miles, and a population of about 3.83 million. As Mr. Dong Xun said in this publication, Japan's area is only 152,300 square miles, but the area of the Four Eastern Provinces is 4,090,000 square miles. Comparing the two, the difference is truly vast.

(1) Liaoning Benxi produces smokeless coal, with an annual output of more than 300,000 tons. Yantai produces smokeless coal, with only a few hundred tons per day. The Fushun mining area extends for five miles and produces more than 11,000 tons per year, all operated by the Benxi Lake Coal and Iron Company. Other gold, silver, talc, and asbestos are also produced. Changbai Mountain is rich in forests, and ginseng is a special product. The Liao River coast produces beans and sorghum, and the coast has the benefit of fish and salt; wild silkworms are produced in the area from Xiuyan to Kuandian.

(2) Jilin Yilan, Ning'an, Mishan, Muling, Dongning, Wangqing, Yanji, Huichun, Hudian, and Panshi are famous gold-producing areas. There are many forests and abundant fur production. Sable fur, ginseng, and Ula grass are the three treasures of Jilin. There is a lot of sorghum, beans, and wheat. Mishan produces a large amount of honey, and Northeast Wang Lake is rich in salt.

(3) Heilongjiang There are four gold mines in Shiwei, and eight gold mines in Qihe. The total gold mining area in Zhongxinggou Hanhe Yu mining area is about 70 li from east to west and 40 li from north to south. The mining bureau is located in Hanhe Laogou. Huma, Yuqinggou, 120 li southeast, has seven locations; North, east, and west are more than 300 li, north and south are more than 100 li, all producing gold, with ten locations, the general bureau is in Taipinggou. The Heihe gold mine has an annual output value of more than 11.1 million yuan. The province's coal mine produces 160 million tons annually. Taking Zhalainuoer as an example, the annual output is more than 200 million catties. The Daxing'anling forest area is 3,000 square li, the Yilehuli forest is 8,000 square li, the Dongxing'anling forest is 6,000 square li, and the Balan area. Bean production is the largest, followed by wheat. The west has the benefits of salt and livestock.

(4) Rehe Mountain gold and placer gold are produced in Chengde, Weichang, Pingquan, Luanping and other counties. Asbestos is produced in Chaoyang and Lingyuan. The province's coal reserves total 930 million tons. Mining is done by the Beipiao Coal Mine Company. Iron is also very rich.

Dear children! After reading about the rich resources of the above four provinces, I hope that you will go and recover them in the future, so as not to let down the purpose of my writing this article.

Children's Works

Watching the "Little Men" Children's Educational Film

— Lin, a sixth-grade student at Jingqin Elementary School

One Sunday afternoon, the weather was clear and bright. Brother Jing led my younger sister Liu Bao and me to the Cathay Grand Theatre to watch a movie.

The movie showing at Cathay that day was "Little Men." Children who love to read this newspaper have already read about it in the education news section of this newspaper. This collection of children's novels is quite famous in the American literary world. Therefore, "Little Men" was jointly starred by thirteen child stars from Hollywood on the silver screen, breaking the unprecedented record in the United States. It was truly a lively and vivid performance.

"Little Men is the most moving story, the most profound description, and the most innocent performance." This sentence is correct. To give a few examples, Natty's introduction to school, the surprise to the point of gratitude, this scene, in the pure emotions of us naive and innocent children, is so fitting! Later, their playing in the circus and the scene of smoking caused the children to fight each other, which also allowed us to transition from a joyful situation to a tragic and tense one. Another scene is when Donn gets money for his friend, puts it in place, and is reprimanded. This is very touching to our heated climax, until Donn runs away, Dickson gets sick and dies, and the burial scene, in particular, make people feel extremely sad.

The story ends like this. In short, "Little Men," this book, "Little Men," this film, is the world of our elementary school students. I hope that all dear children will quickly become familiar with this "Little Men" published in this newspaper, because the content is rich and has great significance in guiding us to good.

Boy Scout Mailbox

Secrets of Camping Answering Miss Zhou Guilian from Beiping

We have thought carefully about what happened to you at the Wo Fo Si (reclining buddha temple) summer camp, and it is entirely because you are not a Girl Scout that you made so many jokes. Now we will tell you.

You said, "Every night the camp gate was not closed tightly, and there was a large gap, and many mosquitoes and gnats came in, biting more than forty wounds on my arm." That is entirely your own fault. Why didn't you buckle the camp gate before staking the tent? Because you staked the tent too far away, the camp gate will naturally have a gap. Has your wound not healed yet? This is again your own fault for not bringing a small first aid kit when camping. Knowing that gnats and mosquitoes in summer are annoying, even at home, ammonia smelling alcohol must be prepared!

Originally, when camping, unless absolutely necessary, do not set up camp in the woods, because even when the weather is sunny, raindrops on the leaves will drip onto the camp, as if it is still raining. Probably your friend did not lie to you, it only rained for half the night, but you thought it rained all night, just because your camp was in the forest, not because there was something wrong with your nerves.

The dew will wet your quilt? We don't quite believe it. We have camped for who knows how many times over the past ten years, and sometimes the camps we used are not as thick as the canvas you used, but we have never been wet with the quilt on our bodies, even in the rain. Let me ask you first, (1) is the tent supported tightly? Is it wrinkled at all? Otherwise, the water will accumulate in the wrinkles or unsupported areas and seep in, and the result will be leakage. (2) Did you firmly remember? Don't let your head, fingers, or anything touch the tent cloth? If you did, it is no wonder that the dew will wet your quilt. Because you touched the tent cloth, the fuzz or fine—fibers—of the cloth were smoothed out, so the water droplets accumulated outside the tent would seep in along the source, and naturally it would leak.

Due to time and space constraints, I cannot fully talk to you here. Soon we will send you another letter directly to discuss the small issues you mentioned.

We of course welcome you to be our friends. Wishing you good health! Respectfully answered by the Chinese Boy Scout Self-Help Society

Call for Articles

This publication's Double Tenth Festival Special Issue is seeking materials such as common sense, poems, jokes, stories, and children's free writings, etc., that are lively and interesting. Each article is limited to a maximum of 400 words. The deadline for submissions is October 4th.

The Seven Sisters in the Mountains (1)

— Xin Qing

In the Westmorland Mountains of England, there is a small and narrow mountain gorge. It is called the Blandthorn Gorge. At its foot lies a green and lovely valley and a Grasmere Lake. The water in the mountain stream flows continuously, flowing from the northern valley area to the lake. In the north, there is also a beautiful valley called Easedale, surrounded by high mountains, covered with green grass. Because there are often groups of sheep grazing there, the grass is soft and smooth, just like the lawn in someone's garden, and in early spring, the grass has grown neatly, as if it is covered with a green velvet carpet, which is unmatched by the hillsides elsewhere. At one end of Easedale, there is a small village called Grasmere Village. At the other end, a sloping high slope leads directly to a small mountain gorge surrounded by high mountains. There is no way out on all sides, only a rugged and uneven low slope that can lead to Easedale. There is also a winding and very dangerous path that passes through the mountains for six miles and reaches the top of Lanthwaite Hill. This lonely mountain gorge is called Far Easedale. A small house stands on the gorge, which is called Blandthorn. There is a crack in the mountain stone above the house, and there is a pool of water outside. There must have been water before, but it has long since dried up.

Living in this small house was an honest old soldier named George Green. He opened up a small farm in the mountains and married a lively and hardworking woman to be his wife. She was good at managing the house and kept the small family in good order. When the weather was clear and the mountain roads were easy to walk, she always dressed her children neatly and sent them to school.

In the winter of 1807, many pieces of furniture were being auctioned off at an estate on Lanthwaite Hill. The residents of the mountains regarded auctions as major events. People from all over the mountains often came from afar and treated each other very politely, using this as an opportunity to do various kinds of business, and old friends who had not seen each other for a long time could also meet and chat. George Green and his wife, Shan Lan, were no exception. They set off early in the morning on this sunny winter day to participate in the auction, leaving their mountain house and six young children to the care of their eldest daughter, Angeni. However, she was only nine years old and could not take care of much. Their family did not employ servants or tenants in the house and fields, and there were no neighbors nearby, so they had to place the heavy responsibility of the family on the shoulders of the nine-year-old girl.

Little Angeni was also a very stable and meticulous child. The day passed peacefully without any unexpected events, but as evening approached, a thick fog covered the mountains, and the air suddenly became suffocating. It was clearly a sign that a major storm was coming. The children earnestly watched for their parents to return, but that day the thick fog blocked their vision, and flakes of snow began to fall. The sky was already dark.
